### [p167_c0002] Standard Follow-Up Report: Transit Adjudication Bureau, 1 st Quarter 2021
[p167_c0003] 
The purpose of this quarterly report is to update the Transit Committee on Transit Adjudication Bureau (TAB) activities and outcomes, as reflected by several Key Indicators.
[p167_c0004] 
TAB is the statutory administrative tribunal that receives, processes, adjudicates and pursues collection of civil penalties arising from the tens of thousands of civil summonses that are issued each year for violations of the Transit Rules of Conduct.
[p167_c0005] 
This quarterly reporting on TAB activities and outcomes commenced in 1992. The report provides the Committee with metrics, covering the most recently completed quarter, for the following Key Indicators:
- [p167_c0006] ‚Ä¢ Number of TAB violations received by TAB ‚Ä¢ Number and dollar amount of payments TAB received ‚Ä¢ TAB revenues and expenses for the quarter ‚Ä¢ Number of cases adjudicated
### [p167_c0007] David Farber
[p167_c0008] 
Vice President and General Counsel, NYC Transit Law Department General Counsel, MTA Bus Company
[p167_c0009] 
_Master Page # 167 of 206 - New York City Transit and Bus Committee Meeting 5/26/2021_

## Page 168

### [p168_c0001] Transit Adjudication Bureau, First Quarter 2021
[p168_c0002] 
The following is a comparison of the key indicators for the first quarter of 2021 as compared to the same period in 2020.
- [p168_c0003] ‚Ä¢ TAB violations issued in the first quarter of 2021 (Q1 2021) decreased by 30.5%, from 42,261 in 2020 to 29,390 in 2021. ‚Ä¢ TAB received 17,024 payments in Q1 2021, a 50.1% decrease from the 34,125 received in Q1 2020. Direct payments decreased by 29.3% (from 21,844 to 15,453) compared to the first quarter of 2020. The number of first quarter payments received from state tax refunds decreased from 12,281 in 2020 to 1,571 in 2021. ‚Ä¢ Total revenue for Q1 2021 was 59.3% lower than in 2020 ($1,708,933 versus $4,199,456). Receipts from direct payments in Q1 2021 decreased by 29.1% ($1,472,917 compared to $2,076,786 in 2020). Receipts from state tax refunds for Q1 2021 relating to outstanding judgments from prior years totaled $268,892, representing an 87.3% decrease from Q1 2020 state tax refund receipts of $2,121,966. ‚Ä¢ TAB revenue for Q1 2021 exceeded expenses by $647,721. This compared to a margin of $3,123,061 for Q1 2020. First quarter expenses decreased by 1.4% relative to 2020 ($1,061,212 compared to $1,076,395).
[p168_c0004] 
For further information, see the Key Indicators Chart on the following page.

http://www.mta.info/nyc/TransitAdjudicationBureau.html

## Page 170

### [p170_c0001] Standard Follow-up Report: Fare Evasion, 1st Quarter 2021
[p170_c0002] 
This report provides fare evasion rates and estimated lost revenue on subways and buses. Note that bus fare evasion is based on data collected using Automatic Passenger Counters (APCs). APCs currently provide robust data for 84% of non-SBS local routes (SBS fare evasion estimates remain based on Eagle Team surveys). The APCs count total ridership which is compared with paid ridership counts to estimate the level of fare evasion.
### [p170_c0003] Subway Fare Evasion Results
[p170_c0004] 
Subway fare evasion in Q1 2021 was 11.3%, 0.4% lower than the 11.7% rate in the 4th quarter. The Q1 2021 revenue loss decreased by $6 million. NYPD enforcement actions increased significantly, up 79% compared with Q4 2020.

### [p175_c0001] Executive Summary
### [p175_c0002] ‚ñ° EEO
[p175_c0003] 
As of March 31, 2021 , there were 48,317 total employees in NYCT's workforce. This represents a 5% decrease from the first quarter 2020 (1Q20).
- [p175_c0004] ‚ñ° Females represented 19% (9,014) of our workforce and remained constant when compared to 1Q20 possibly due to hiring restrictions and attrition. ‚ñ° Females were hired above their current representation possibly due to recruitment outreach efforts targeting females to fill vacancies in operating titles. ‚ñ° Minorities represented 79% (38,386) of our workforce, and remained constant compared to 1Q20 possibly due to hiring restrictions and attrition. ‚ñ° Minorities were hired above their current representation due to ongoing yet limited hiring in the critical operating vacancies that were filled.

## Page 179

### [p179_c0001] Definitions of EEO Job Categories
### [p179_c0002] Officials & Administrators
[p179_c0003] 
Occupations in which employees set broad policies, exercise overall responsibility for execution of these policies, or direct individual departments or special phases of the agency's operations, or provide specialized consultation on a regional, district or area basis.
### [p179_c0004] Professionals
[p179_c0005] 
Occupations which require specialized and theoretical knowledge which is usually acquired through college training or through work experience and other training which provides comparable knowledge.
### [p179_c0006] Technicians
[p179_c0007] 
Occupations which require a combination of basic scientific or technical knowledge and manual skill which can be obtained through specialized post-secondary school education or through equivalent on-the-job training.
### [p179_c0008] Protective Services
[p179_c0009] 
Occupations in which workers are entrusted with public safety, security and protection from destructive forces.
### [p179_c0010] Paraprofessionals
[p179_c0011] 
Occupations in which workers perform some of the duties of a professional or technician in a supportive role, which usually require less formal training and/or experience normally required for professional or technical status.
### [p179_c0012] Administrative Support
[p179_c0013] 
Occupations in which workers are responsible for internal and external communication, recording and retrieval of data and/or information and other paperwork required in an office.
### [p179_c0014] Skilled Craft
[p179_c0015] 
Occupations in which workers perform jobs which require special manual skill and a thorough and comprehensive knowledge of the process involved in the work which is acquired through on-the-job training and experience or through apprenticeship or other formal training programs.
### [p179_c0016] Service Maintenance
[p179_c0017] 
Occupations in which workers perform duties which result in or contribute to the comfort, convenience, hygiene or safety of the general public or which contribute to the upkeep and care of buildings, facilities or grounds of public property.
[p179_c0018] 
_Master Page # 179 of 206 - New York City Transit and Bus Committee Meeting 5/26/2021_

## Page 193

### [p193_c0001] Executive Summary
### [p193_c0002] ‚ñÝ Diversity Initiatives to increasing representation
[p193_c0003] 
MTA Bus diversify recruitment strategy showed its resilience in 2020 by leading and/or participating in out a sizable number of diversity recruiting programs that support our ability to attract, advance, and retrain minorities, females, veterans and persons with disabilities.
[p193_c0004] 
In the first quarter, we focused on improving the representation of women and minorities in our managerial ranks by holding a Superintendent of Transportation panel discussion where potential job candidates could get a realistic preview of this first-level management job.
[p193_c0005] 
MTA Bus also established partnerships with several new recruitment sources such as Catalyst, National & Disability Council, Jobs for Humanity, and Young Adult Institute (YAI).
[p193_c0006] 
One of the new recruitment source, Jobs for Humanity, is a global organization that connects persons with disabilities and underrepresented communities to job opportunities. The organization offered MTA Bus the opportunity to post jobs on its website at no cost. Another recruitment source, YAI, offered MTA Bus the opportunity to attend free workshops online to learn more about people with disabilities. The organization also offered to provide sensitivity training.
[p193_c0007] 
_Master Page # 193 of 206 - New York City Transit and Bus Committee Meeting 5/26/2021_

## Page 195

### [p195_c0001] Definitions of EEO Job Categories
### [p195_c0002] Officials & Administrators
[p195_c0003] 
Occupations in which employees set broad policies, exercise overall responsibility for execution of these policies, or direct individual departments or special phases of the agency's operations, or provide specialized consultation on a regional, district or area basis.
### [p195_c0004] Professionals
[p195_c0005] 
Occupations which require specialized and theoretical knowledge which is usually acquired through college training or through work experience and other training which provides comparable knowledge.
### [p195_c0006] Technicians
[p195_c0007] 
Occupations which require a combination of basic scientific or technical knowledge and manual skill which can be obtained through specialized post-secondary school education or through equivalent on-the-job training.
### [p195_c0008] Protective Services
[p195_c0009] 
Occupations in which workers are entrusted with public safety, security and protection from destructive forces.
### [p195_c0010] Paraprofessionals
[p195_c0011] 
Occupations in which workers perform some of the duties of a professional or technician in a supportive role, which usually require less formal training and/or experience normally required for professional or technical status.
### [p195_c0012] Administrative Support
[p195_c0013] 
Occupations in which workers are responsible for internal and external communication, recording and retrieval of data and/or information and other paperwork required in an office.
### [p195_c0014] Skilled Craft
[p195_c0015] 
Occupations in which workers perform jobs which require special manual skill and a thorough and comprehensive knowledge of the process involved in the work which is acquired through on-the-job training and experience or through apprenticeship or other formal training programs.
### [p195_c0016] Service Maintenance
[p195_c0017] 
Occupations in which workers perform duties which result in or contribute to the comfort, convenience, hygiene or safety of the general public or which contribute to the upkeep and care of buildings, facilities or grounds of public property.
[p195_c0018] 
_Master Page # 195 of 206 - New York City Transit and Bus Committee Meeting 5/26/2021_

## Page 198

### [p198_c0001] Underutilization Analysis Overview
[p198_c0002] 
A utilization analysis was conducted to determine whether there is underutilization of females and minorities in its workforce. This analysis consists of comparing March 31, 2021 workforce percentages for females and minorities to 80 percent of the females and minorities available within the relevant labor market. Underutilization exists if the percentage of females or minorities in a job category is less than 80 percent of their expected estimated availability.
[p198_c0003] 
The following chart provide shaded/bolded areas that represent below 80 percent of the Census availability or underutilization: (1) the female and minority workforce percentages for this agency; (2) 80 percent of the females and minorities available for work based on the 2010 Census by job category; and (3) whether or not the estimated availability percentages were met for females and minorities within each of the job categories.
[p198_c0004]
